This is a fundamental protocol used for transferring data, including web pages, over the internet. This is a fundamental protocol used for transferring data, including web pages, over the internet. It's a crucial part of how the web works, allowing different systems to communicate with each other and exchange information.

In the context of web addresses, HTTP is often seen at the beginning of a URL, preceding the website's domain name. For example, "http://www.example.com" is a complete URL, where "http" specifies the protocol used to access the website. This protocol defines how messages are formatted and transmitted, as well as how the client (usually a web browser) and server respond to each other.

It's worth noting that there's also a secure version of this protocol, called HTTPS (HyperText Transfer Protocol Secure), which adds an extra layer of security by encrypting the data being transmitted. This is especially important for websites that handle sensitive information, such as passwords or credit card numbers.
